CONSTRUCTION MANAGEMENT
FRAMEWORK

Construction is a process of a building or assembling of infrastructure.
The construction project is a construct of infrastructure within the
budget, time and quality. Essential planning, proper design, and well-
planned execution are required for the construction projects. There are
various types of construction like building construction, industrial
construction, infrastructure construction, and heavy construction

1. Construction projects are change-oriented and self-managed.

With the accelerated change in the environment, management of
multi-discipline, multi-dimensional, multi-location multi-national
tasks needs project management philosophy different from the
traditional functional organizational structures of the ongoing
industrial establishments.

Ever since the dawn of civilization, man has indulged in some form of
construction activity. Even in ancient times, man created architectural
marvels, which in turn regarded as a wonder of the world. The
pyramids of Egypt, Great Wall of China, TajMahal in India, Hanging
Gardens of Babylon, Leaning Tower of Pisa in Italy, temples of
Cambodia are such examples.

History of construction effort in Nepal
If we analyze the construction efforts in Nepal, we found that the first

attempt was made in the name of 'Banaune Adda’ or construction
bureau, in 1769 During the Rana Regime (1846 — 1951) A.D

which was extended its departments to the various parts of the
country. It maintained the royal palace, government buildings, and
undertook new construction works. In this period, there was ‘Public
Works MadhesPahad Report NiksariAdda’ (PWMPRNA), whose
office was at Bhadrakali of Kathmandu. This looked after construction
works outside the Kathmandu Valley. Likewise, construction works in
the Kathmandu valley were controlled by ‘Sadar Public Nikasi Adda’
or the Central Public Works Bureau. In 1934 A.D, a new department
Jana SevaBibhag or public Service Department was set up to perform
the civic works, tasks of municipalities: water supply, sewerage, street
roads, lighting, etc. in municipal towns. The Rana regime lasted till
1951 A.D when it was replaced by a democratic government. In the
same time, the Ministry of Transport was formed and it was

responsible for.construction works. |
‘no structure built-in Nepal was an iron bridge over
first public water supply system was
laid in Kathmandu valley during 1888- 1895 A.D. The royal palace,

the clock tower and the suspension bridge on the river i a“
were built during these years. The first hydro-electric projec at

Pharphing- was completed in 1911 A.D. The Rost 2a
Railway Jine by M/s Marti ee Co. Ltd_of Calcutta and fe
Matatirtha Ropeway by M/s Keyner Son and'Co. of Loncon were

Role of Construction Industry in National Economy
The construction industry is one of th

economy. Its contribution to the GDP and employment is very
significant and plays an important role in the development of
infrastructure that is essential for the development of all other sectors.
In Nepal, more than 10 percent of the GDP is contributed by the
construction sector and is one of the largest employers. It is estimated
that this sector is-ereating employment opportunities for more than

one million people in the country. Nepalese Contractors are now
saving a huge amount of foreign currency from its flight to abroad by
foreign contractors. So it is contributing to export industries to the
national economy. Therefore any enhance

ment made to this sector
will have a positive impact on the national economy. In developing

countries, about 60 ercent tional bud is allocated on

development works and a significant portion of the development
budget is allocated to the construction sector in Nepal.

e important: sectors in any

Physical infrastructure development is the major tools that led to
prosperous and developed nations. National infrastructure system
must be connected through global and regional links if a country is to
benefit from the expansion of markets and trade through globalization.
Infrastructure development offers the foundation on which a country
can seize and capitalize on the opportunities ushered in by
globalization and regional integration.

Investments in large scale infrastructures are critical to enabling a
country to achieve long term growth and sustainable poverty
reduction. It played an important role in enabling the poor to
Participate in the growth process. Access to education and health
which are also the indicators of economic development can be vastly
improved through better road, electricity, communications, water
Supply, and sanitation services.

Construction management is an emerging new scope of management.
The world is seeking of good construction managers. International and
domestic construction markets are the major scope in present days.
The market of the construction business in both international as well

economy. Nepal is still lacking sufficient road network. If road

regard to attract the private sector to make investments in the road
sector following the Built, Operate and Transfer (BOT) approach.

2. Irrigation and Hydropower cae (a >

Nepal is the second richest country after Brazil in its water resource
and it has great prospects in generating hydroelectricity and
constructing irrigation projects throughout the country. Although
Nepal has a large reserve of water resources, it is not able to utilize
them properly. At the end of FY 2072/73, the total peak demand is
around 1423 (MW) provisional but the power production is less than
the demand. Hydropower production is around 829 MW only, which
is merely 0.85 percent of the total potentiality of 83,000 MW. So there
is a wider scope of hydroelectricity market inside the nation and the
possibility of exporting to India as well.

1.3 Construction Project Characteristics

(7A project is defined as a temporary endeavor undertaken to create a

new product or service to achieve specified objectives within the
assigned resources) A project is a mission. Projects are usually a part
of an overall, strategic program. A program at the macro level
comprises one or more projects. Some examples of construction
projects include:
e Constructing a building or facility. -
e Developing a new product or service.
e Designing a new transportation system.
In general, the termf'construction project’ refers to a high-value, time-
bound, special construction mission with pre-determined performance_
objectiv Construction projects employ huge. ‘TesOUTCeS of men,
materials, and » machines. The construction project mission is

different stages of the life cycle. Project risks can be related to
time, costs, technology, scope and performance.

7. Resource Integration: Projects consume and coordinate
resources. A project integrates physical, financial, human
information. It maintains appropriate interrelationships with
them. Resource use is prioritized in a a disciplined way for
optimization.

g. Planning and Control: Projects work to a plan. A project
requires effective and efficient planning and control systems.
Standards are set for project-activities-through planning. They
Serve as yardsticks for measuring project performance. Us
performance is.compared with standards to find out deviations.
Corrective actions are taken to control deviations.

9. Contracting and sub-contracting: Most projects are contract...
based. The project work is characterized by a high level of
contracting and subcontracting. Contracts can be: of various
types, such as lump-...sum_..contract, unit_price__contrack

negotiated cost, plus fixed fee contract and turnkey contract,
“Proper contract planning and management is the key to effective
project management.

10. Beneficiaries: All projects have beneficiaries. Beneficiaries are
the ultimate users of the project outputs. They are the client of
the project. A project has a specific group of beneficiaries. It
should be focused on fulfilling or exceeding their requirements.
Projects should clearly identify the needs of their beneficiaries.

b. Project Categories (, C205 £) ( comaroeh foul \nta

u4

business.

Planning by Contractor
a. Pre-construction stage planning
The planning undertaken by the contractor after receipt of tender
notice and before submitting the bid is known as pre-construction or ®
tender stage planning. Steps of planning at this stage are as follows: on
e Careful Study of tender documents to find out the scope of
work and employer’s requirement.

Study of drawings and Bill of Quantities (BOQ) to find out
the quantities of each item of wor

Study of Specifications to find out the quality of materials and
work required.

Site visit~and_investigation to determine the availability of
construction materials at site or nearby site (if required).

Determine the method | of _workexecution i.e. by labor or

equipment
b. Construction stage planning

After the acceptance of the tender, the contractor further needs in-
depth planning. This stage of planning is also known as contract
planning. Here are the following steps in this stage of planning:
e Site mobilization
e Working out detailed quantities of materials required and
fixing the methods of procurement and sources of them
Working out detailed about construction_workforce like
skilled and unskilled manpower
Working out details of plants, equipment their layout and
repair & maintenance strategy
Planning for camp facilities, access, accommodations, site
<< SO Sea eee
_ offices and layout

se of scheduling

ollowing are the use of scheduling
The quantity of work involved, labor, material, equipment and
money required at each stage of work can be determined.
The actual progress of the. work can be monitored and
controlled from time to time.

Advantages of scheduling
Following are the advantages of scheduling
e By studying the schedule of work, alternative methods of
execution can be examined and the most economical method
can be selected. Further, the effect of likely constraints can be
evaluated at the planning stage.
It gives a clear picture of quantity.and type. of materials,
manpower, machines at different stages of construction.
As the time of starting of an activity is known, the
arrangements of adequate resources can be done in advance
urce_utilization can be optimized
The actual progress of each activity can be evaluated with
reference to the planned program
The interrelationship between the activities. is known hence
their priorities can be set up
e Application of value engineering can be adopted. -
Classification of scheduling i pe prea. cle to FE
Construction planning and scheduling require the supply of materials,
engagement of labors, completing the activities or operations and the
time when the equipment or machinery is to be employed. These are
known as ‘material’,’ labor’, ‘construction’, ‘equipment’ and
‘financial’ schedules.
Construction schedule and its preparation
Before preparing the construction schedule, the following information
must be known
¢ Various operations to be done in a particular project
* Quantum of works to be done in each operation

Labor schedule

The aim of this schedule is to determine the number of, skilled and
unskilled labor required for the execution of different operations on
different dates. With the help of this schedule required labor can be
arranged well in time. It is difficult and costly to arrange labor when
required. It helps in reducing the labor cost. A labor schedule can be
prepared from the construction schedule.

Equipment schedule

To decide the type, number and dates on which particular equipment
will be needed, equipment use schedule has to be prepared before the
Start of the project, so it is arranged well in advance and brought at the
Site as and when needed. The aim of this schedule is to derive the
maxi age of the equipment when at the site and remove it
er This will save money.

ilestone Charts
ilestones mark significant events in the life_of a project, usually
critical activities which must be achieved on time to avoid delay in the

project. fe

deadlines (avoid using intermediate stages).

Gantt Charts

A Gantt chart is a horizontal bar or line chart which commonly

include the following features:

¢ activities identified on the left-hand side;

° time scaleis drawn on the top (or bottom) of the chart;

e a horizontal bar or a line is drawn against each activity
indicating estimated duration;

e dependencies between activities are shown;

ritical Path

Project cost

For any project total expenditure incurred in terms of manpower,
©quipment, machinery, materials and time to achieve a particular goal

is known as the total cost of the project. The total cost of the project is
the sum of two distinct costs.

° Direct cost
* Indirect cost

a Cost of materials, equipment, and money spent on manpower form
i direct cost. The direct costs of a project are of major concern and
‘ior pattern of direct costs with time is of importance. The direct

aration is not linear,

Minimum duration

The duration obtained after crashing all activities (maximum possible
extent) is known as minimum duration.

Time cost trade-off

Time and cost are the two most important resources that a project
manager deals with. Both of these resources have constrained and the
job of a project manager is to have a judicious balance between them.
The judicious balance between time and cost is called Time-Cost
trade-off and it can be achieved by studying the availability and
demand of these resources for the given project.

eae First of all, draw the network diagram and find out all

i ossible paths. Critical path and non-critical paths. critics
path duration is the normal project duration for that DI
Calculate the direct cost by adding the normal cost of a
activities. Calculate indirect cost by multiplying project
duration with the indirect cost (overhead or indirect expense)
per unit time.

Calculate the cost slopes of all activities
ascending order of cost slopes.

- Start crashing the project from a critical path (since this is the
project duration) by selecting such critical activity having
least cost slope as per ranking to the maximum possible extent
(observe other non-critical paths which are likely to be
critical)

Calculate the direct cost by adding the extra cost of crashing
(cost slope times (Tn-Tc)) required for crashing that activity
to the direct cost calculated in previous steps and
corresponding indirect cost of reduced project duration.

6. After this step three possible cases may arise:

The case I: If the same path remains critical (longest) then crashing is
onsidered for the critical activity serially in the ascending order to
their cost slope as far as possible.

Case II: While crashing the critical path, there may emerge a new
critical path/s then crashing is carried out for the common activity. If
there is more than one common activity, activity with the least cost
slope is selected first and continues serially as per the ranking of cost
slopes.

and rank them in

Case Ill: After crashing as per the case II, if there is a possibility of

crashing then, one activity from each path is selected at one time for

crashing. This crashing is known as simultaneous crashing or parallel

eit The process is continued until the project shortening is
SS1DIe.

Ne time after crashing, the direct cost and indirect cost is calculated
0 find out the total cost. If the total cost calculated after crashing is
greater than the earlier step, we come to the end of optimization.

Mine for the determination of minimum possible time (Tm),
ashing should be continued until the possibility.

ment for Finishing of Concrete

Equip
infer compaction of concrete, the concrete surface is finished by

15 Cranes for Lifting

Hoisting is the operation of lifting the load from one location,
transporting it to another location situated at a reasonable distance and
landing it down. Cranes are the versatile and most useful machine. It
is the only single machine capable of providing three-dimensional
Movements to a load virtually in one continuous operation. It is able to
perform the operations with speed, safety, and precision. It is
becessary to know the lifting capacity and working range of a crane to
deselected to perform a given job.

F Equipment f )
~ Construction

ighway construction involves earthwork in excavation, embankment
onstruction, and pavement construction. The equipment used in the

onstructions of pavements is discussed below.

Sub-grade Preparation and compaction

he subgrade is prepared after earthwork in the excavation.

Preparation of subgrade includes site clearance, grading, and
compaction. A grader is used to grade the surface to achieve uniform
surface both along the cross section and longitudinal section. Final
ompaction of the subgrade is done with the help of compacting
equipment like rollers, sheep foot tandem roller carefully so that sd
rollers, tandem rollers, pneumatic tired rollers, etc.

Construction of sub-base and compaction

After achieving the final and finished surface of subgrade, subbase is

prepared. Sub-base construction involves quarrying of sub-base
Materials, screening of sub-base materials, transporting the materials

to the site and spread by loader or grader and compact the sub-base in

layers. The top surface is graded with the help of grader to bring it
to the final surface. Final compaction is then done with the help of
Ompacting equipment.

nstruction of Base-course

Free Account" means any construction work to be carried out by a
lic Entity itself. It is the execution of public works by using the
nurces of a public agency of the government, without recourse to
mpetitive bidding or negotiated contract. Works done by force
ount may apply in the following situation:

The Size, nature, and location of the works being unsuitable for
competitive bidding.

Works must be carried out without disrupting existing
operations, by crews familiar with those operations.

When the implementing agency can bear the associated risks in
a better way than the contractor.

No contractor is interested in carrying out the works.

2. Consideration
It is the cause, motive, price or impelling influence that induces
contracting party to enter into a contract. Consideration can be
described as something of value that is exchanged by th
contracting parties.
3. Capacity to contract
For a contract to be legally binding and enforceable, all parties
must be capable to enter into a contract. As per the contract act, the
following persons are not capable of contract. Idiots, drunkards,
insane, and children below 16 years are not capable of signing the
contract.

4. Lawful purpose

_ An illegal contract is invalid. If two parties agree to perform a job.
vi hich i is against the country law, the contract is invalid.

Possibility of performance

ie impossible contract is invalid. If two parties agree to build?
Se on air, which is impossible, the contract is invalid.

Ze consent

he contract should not involve coercion, fraud, undue influen®

feceit. Otherwise, the contract is invalid.

Certainty/ uncertainty

_ The contract which cannot be carried out because of va

reasons (vague/ ambiguous etc.) are not valid.

1 Classification by the method of payment for the work

The method of payment is of such importance, particularly to the
Contractor, that contracts are often classified solely by the method of
payment. There are three basic methods of payment used in

Engineering Contracts:
e Lump-sum contracts
e Schedule of rates or unit-price contracts

e Cost-plus contracts

Sometimes, Part Lump Sum and Part Unit-Price Contract is also
adopted in a single project as a fourth type also. The Lump Sum and
the Unit-Price Contracts may be either “fixed” or “subject to cost
adjustment” as specified in the contract.

This is the oldest form of fee structure. This form is very lucrative
he contractor but is subject to abuse. There is little incentive t0 be
efficient and economical in the construction of the project. Just to the
ontrary, the larger the cost of the job, the higher the amount of
hat is paid by the owner. If the cost of the job is Rs.40 million and the :

ee is 2%, then the contractor’s fee is Rs.800,000. If the cost increase gen

nla, it is common to specify a target price for the total contract. If
m tractor brings the job in under the target, the savings are
tt or shared between the owner and contractor. A common
givide formula provides that the contractor shares by getting 25% of
shart id run of the target. If for instance, the target is Rs.10 Million
BF ic contractor completes the job in Rs 9.5 Million, he receives a
ponus of RS.125,000.
y, Cost + Sliding Fee : Ms
i variation of the profit-sharing approach is the sliding fee, which not
only provides a bonus for underrun but also penalizes the contractor
or overrunning the target value. The amount of fee increases as the
ontractor falls below the target and decreases as he overruns the
arget value. One formula for calculating the contractor’s fee based on
a sliding scale is,
Fee = R (2T-A)
Where,
= Target price

ntages

Promotion of private investment.

parison of Turn-key and BOOT Projects

BOOT projects are contractor financed turnkey contracts.
BOOT project strategies grew out of turnkey contracting.

In conventional turnkey contracts, governments have
attempted to shift the risk for the project construction to the
private sector while still bearing the risk of financing and
operating the project. In a concession project ie. BOOT
project, the major risks of finance and operation, however,
borne by the promoter.

* In turnkey contracts, feasibility studies are often carried out
by the principal while in BOOT project, the promoter will be
responsible for feasibility studies.

Commercialization of a turnkey contract is normally the
responsibility of the principal, who will often pay the
contractor a mobilization fee and monthly payments for the
work carried out. In BOOT projects, the promoter will carry
out commercialization.

In turnkey contracts, operation of the facility is carried out by
the principal after one or two years of commissioning while in
BOOT projects, the promoter will operate the facility over the
Concession period before finally transferring the facility to the
Principal.

ii) Two-Stage Bidding Procedure
en it is not feasible to define fully the technical aspects of the
pods oF construction works or services to be procured or the terms
and conditions of the procurement contract at the time of the invitation

to bid.

* stage

. ~ The bidding documents shall state the purpose of
procurement, expected performance, broad specifications, and
other broad features and the qualification of bidders.

- Bidders are requested not to quote the price but shall submit
only technical proposal and comments on the terms and
conditions of the proposed procurement contract.

* Hold discussions with any or all bidders in relation to the bids
submitted in response to the invitation

- Modifying or improving the technical specifications,
evaluation criteria and terms and conditions of the
procurement contract in order to increase competition,

* Determining the evaluation system in order to determine the
appropriateness of various options submitted by the bidders

2” stage

* After the completion of the 1“ as referred previously,
invitation to second stage bid is made. In making such
invitation to bid, the bidders whose bids have not been
cancelled from 1 stage shall be invited to submit bid along
with price in accordance with revised bidding documents.

Sprequalification as

e successful execution of contracts for large and complex buildings,
ivil engineering, supply and installation, turnkey, and design and
uild projects requires that contracts are awarded only to those firms,
combinations of firms, that are suitably experienced in the type of
ork and construction technology involved, that are financially and
anagerially sound, and that can provide all the equipment required in
timely manner. The assessment by an implementing agency of the
itability of firms to carry out a particular contract prior to being
vited to submit a bid is a process called Pre-Qualification.

is a kind of shortlisting of the eligible bidder to avoid crowding of
e bidder. It ensures that the invitation to bids extended only to those
Ospective bidders who have adequate capacity and resources to
tform the particular contract satisfactory taking in to account their-

Disadvantages of Pre-qualification

On the negative side, prequalification has some potential
disadvantages:

(a) It may increase procurement lead time, although this can be
minimized by good procurement scheduling, e.g., undertaking
the prequalification process while bid documents are being
prepared;

(b) The Employer is required to review all prequalification
applications, whereas post-qualification requires the review of
the qualifications of, normally, only one (the lowest
evaluated) bidder;

Collusion (and the possibility of price-rigging) is easier
among a limited number of identified bidders, particularly if
they are of the same nationality;

The element of subjective judgment required by evaluators
when applying the prequalification criteria to a number of
Applicants, and’ the discretionary rights reserved to the
pacts: provide opportunities for externally influenced
ales from the expected high standards of ethics and
A mpartiality in prequalifying applicants.

in evaluating and comparing a bid, the comparison shall have to be
made by fixing the quoted price excluding Value Added Tax. The
evaluation committee shall have to evaluate the bid included for

e If any arithmetical error is found in a bid, the Public Entity
may correct such an error, and where, in making such
correction, there exists a discrepancy between unit rate and
total amount, the unit rate shall prevail, and the total amount
shall be corrected as per the same rate.

¢ Where there is a discrepancy between figures and words in a
bid submitted by a bidder, the amount in words shall prevail.

Liquidated Damages

Liguidated (delay) Damages are remedies available to any contracting
party to compensate for the financial loss suffered as the result of a
proven breach of contract. In Common Law Countries, it is known as
liquidated damages. In Civil Law Countries, it is known as
Contractual Penalties. Its amount is designate during the formation of
a 4contract for the injured party to collect as compensation upon a
ime to Specific breach. If the works under the procurement contract fail to be

fe sompleted Within the time specified in the contract due to the delay of
ae consultant, service provider or construction entrepreneur
five percent Ch eet en damages, generally of zero decimal zero

pending upon the type ieee Hence claim mad | :
antractOt need not necessarily be the exact amount mentioned in th
contract. , ’ -She ioe
rovisional sum need not be always allocated specifically for a single
Hck. Sometimes part of the contract itself may be made a provisional

mm, There can be one or more than one provisional sum item ina
eontract. To elaborate, let us take the example of site clearance. There
Fay be so many unpredictable Items in site clearance. Consider an
infrastructure project involving flyover, roads, ete. wherein the regular
tems of clearance include asphalt road, paving blocks, kerb, signal
poles, crash barriers, guard rails, signboards, stormwater drainage
pipelines, sewerage pipelines, manholes, catch pits, gullies, trees,
pushes, shrubs, buildings, fencing, compound walls, sculptures and
monuments, concrete structures etc. In addition, there will be items
specific to the site as well. Many items will be measurable at the time
of tender but some of them turn out to be uncertain. For example, the
quantum of work involved in the removal of a site-specific item like
Sculpture or monument may become difficult to ascertain. One way to
overcome this difficulty is to allocate these as a separate provisional
sum item in the BOQ.

In respect of every Provisional Sum, the Engineer shall have authority
10 issue instructions for the execution of work or for the supply of
800ds, materials, Plant or services. :

a tems that can be included in PS are lab test, insurance, OSH,
Nt for the construction of the site office, environmental and
safeguards, purchasing of the survey instrument, etc.

Contingencies are clauses in a contract that Be Oe pe uy fis an cae ted Y
seller a way to get out of the contract if certain * Le e stl sssocl she
are not met. A commonly used example is that 0 , y' Thee i 008 da? rt
offer on a new home before selling his existing sea buyer ss jee
needs to sell his present home before being able to get cing on F, hare t a =
the new one. Therefore, he makes his offer contingent upon the sale soil ‘et 108 joit
of his existing home. There will always be a time period associated one P10) sans of mi
1. with such a contingency. If the buyer is able to get his present home oj i rile joint
_____ Sold within that'time period, the deal can go forward. But if he fails to sve W i oséitl
sell within the specified time period, the seller has the option of corporations also us

getting out of the deal. In most cases, sellers will not accept this kind
of contingency, because they will most likely feel that they can find
another buyer capable of closing the deal without needing to sell
another home first. But new home builders are often willing to accept
an offer contingent upon the sale of an existing home. The
contingencies in public project are limited to four (4) percent of the
estimated cost. The four (4) percent is divided into two (2) percent
» - cach for work charge establishment and minor physical contingencies.

joint Venture (JV)

{joint venture (JV) is a business arrangement in which two or more
narties agree to pool their resources for accomplishing a Specific task
This task can be a new project or any other business activity, In a joint
enture (JV), each of the participants is responsible for Profits, losses
ind costs associated with it. However, the venture is its own entity,
geparate and apart from the participants’ other business interests.

On account, The :
the work. vate neither

A joint venture takes place when two parties com
ne project. In a joint venture, both parties are equally invested in the
project in terms of money, time, and effort to build on the original
soncept. While joint ventures are generally small projects, major
orporations also use this method in order to diversify. A joint venture
an ensure the success of smaller projects for those that are just
farting in the business world or for established corporations. Since
he cost of starting new projects is generally high, a joint venture

lows both parties to share the burden of the project, as well as the
sulting profits.

€ together to take on

alue-Added Tax (VAT) is a tax on consumer spending. It is
bllected by VAT-registered traders on their supplies of goods and
vices effected within the State, for consideration, to their
tomers. A type of consumption tax that is placed on a product
henever the value is added at a stage of production and at final sale.

Line of Credit (LC)

A line of credit is basically a flexible loan from a bank or financial
institution to an individual or business. Not unlike how a credit card
offers you a limited amount of funds that you can use when, if, and
how you wish, a line of credit is a limited/spécified amount of mo
that an individual can access as needed and then repay immediately or
over a pre-specified period of time. Like a loan, a line of credit will
charge interest as soon as money is borrowed, and borrowers must be
approved by the bank (and such approval is a byproduct of the
_ borrower's credit rating and/or relationship with the bank). A line of
credit is any credit source extended to a government, business
or individual by a bank or other financial institution. A line of credit
may take several. forms, such as overdraft Protection, demand loan,
special purpose, export packing credit, term loan, discounting,
purchase of commercial bills, _ traditional revolving credit
card account, etc. It is effectively a source of funds that can readily be

- Interest is paid only on money

Variation Order (VO)

After having started the work in accordance with the procurement
contract, if there is required the addition to and reduction in the
quantity or addition of a new item to or substitution in such work due
fo technical reasons, the competent authority may issue a variation
order for a variation of up to fifteen percent.

Fnonsive the system can be to changes in product or service

; a facility is arranged in order to maximize processes that are
t efficient but effective towards the overall organizational goal.
Fic requirements of construction job mainly man, material, the
be must be controlled and placed at a site in such a manner that

Machines are placed in the most advantageous position.
Materials are placed/stored near the place of their utilization
General site circulation to manpower is orderly and their site

accommodation is available

Bsic objective of the layout decision is to ensure a smooth flow

Tk, material, people, and information through the system.
ve layouts also:

Minimize material handling costs;
Utilize space efficiently;

Utilize labor efficiently;

Eliminate bottlenecks;

Facilitate communication and interaction between workers,

between workers and their supervisors, OF between workers
and customers;

Reduce manufacturing cycle time and customer service time;

Eliminate wasted or redundant movement;

Facilitate the entry, exit, and placement of material, products,

Nature and type of work: nature and type of work play a

"crucial role in the job layout plan. Every construction projects

are unique in nature. For example, the job layout plan for the

construction of the headworks in a hydropower project is

definitely different from the job layout plan for the

construction of the building project.

Access to the site: the access to the site does facilitate the

transportation of the construction materials and equipment at

minimum cost.

Nature of ground: for the equipment fixing and movement,

we need the solid ground.

Temporary roads: the temporary road from the nearest road

head to the site must be constructed before Starting the

construction activity for the efficient transportation

Construction methods: the methods of construction is

essential for job layout. For example, job layout in precast or

prefab needs extra casting yard whereas cast in situ does not

need it.

Construction material: if the construction material is

available naturally nearest the site, then no need to worry for

the storage otherwise the storage of construction material

should be carried out in job layout plan

terial Handling is concerned with solving the pragmatic problems
olving the movement, storage, control and protection of materials,
sds and products throughout the processes of cleaning, preparation,
nufacturing, distribution, consumption, and disposal. The focus of
dies of Material Handling course work is on the methods,
chanical equipment, systems and related controls used to achieve
se functions. :

e Materials are of various nature — some need to be stored under
roof, some in open area and some need to be stored very
carefully as they are volatile and dangerous to be used by ©
common people

Materials are stored in such a quantity which can run-up to the
day on which material can be delivered in the site from the
date of order. i
Indent forms are used to get material at the site. The indent is
kept in a book form and page number. Indenting officer fills
the indent form and sends the form with a blank invoice to the
issuing officer, who is in charge of stock.

The issuing officer checks the quantity available in the stock
and can correct the quantity, fill in the indent form with actual
quantity and send the corrected invoice to the demanding
officer for signature. The receiving officer signs the invoices
and sends back to issuing officer as an acknowledgment of the
receipt,

Financial Managemen > ae
s one of the most useful instruments of transaction. It Play
Money is on verybody life and every activity of indi

;mportant role in & ; : + jet
eres and government. For a construction business, it is

for production, distribution and to contribute to the development ,
the country. The propet managemen
Finance refers to funds needed by

governments rs

Finance studies money and its management, and like economics, it
explores the allocation of resources, the process of money
management. Firms invest money in plants and equipment but retums
are earned in the future. If the individual manages the money for him
then this is called personnel finance. Management of money within
government is public finance, whereas money manages within the
construction business can be considered as corporate finance. The
study of corporate finance raises the theme of financial managers who
has great responsibilities in managing the cash and funds within the
construction project. The financial managers must make certain that
the firm can meet its obligations as they came due, determine which
are best sources of financing for the firm, and allocate the firm's
resources among competing for investment alternatives. They a
responsible for acquiring funds needed by a firm and for directing

those funds into projects that will maximize the value of the firm 1!
its Owners.

aging cash flow is extremely an important task of financial
gnagers because the primary goal of financial managers is to
sximize a firm's value and is based on its cash flows. The financial
pnager's task is determining how much cash a firm should have on
md at any time to ensure normal business operations continue
thout interruption. If a firm holds more cash than its need,
areholders returns will not be maximized.

ash management assumes more important than other current assets
scause cash is the most significant and the least productive asset that
firm holds. The aim of cash management should maintain adequate
sh position to keep the firm sufficiently liquid and to use excess
ash in some profitable way. Therefore, the financial manager should
y to maintain the optimum level of cash that maximizes the value of

e firm.

sash flow Forecasting of Contractor

Even though the regular and interim payments are made as per the
rovision in the contract between client and contractor, both parties
ometimes do face the liquidity problem. Shortage of funds affects the
ogress of the project in turn can lead to the stoppage of work.

fhe project funding pattern can be determined by making a cash flow
recast that predicts the monthly net effect of the cash inflow and
flow. Client cash flow study is to forecast the extent of the funds
equired periodically for meeting payment commitments. Contractor’s
ash flow forecast is more complex and detailed, as it has to cater to
a inflows and outflows. Cash inflow is deterrhined to form the
Mject’s revenue receipts in terms of earned values budget. Cash
4 determination needs extensive and in-depth analysis of
hater) ‘ia budget heads like working capital, equipment, and

Creating quality consciousness,

The materials accounting process from the demand initiation stage till
is consumption stage involves the maintenance of up-to-date records
of receipts and issues at the project central store, monthly stock
checking of materials in the store and at the worksite and the return of
unused materials after the completion of the intended job.

Wastage of materials can take place during the proc
during storage, and during its utilization.
I Wastage during procurement can result from on
following main causes: u

(a)
(b) Buying more than the actual requirements.
I (c) Unnecessary buying of items to cater
unforeseen eventualities.
(d) Untimely buying of short-lived materials. ‘"
(e) Improper and unnecessary handling of materials
(f) | Wastage in transportation. le

* Cost Variance Percent (CVP) = (CV/BCWP) x 100 %
* Schedule Variance Percent (SVP) = (SV/BCWS) x 100%
* Schedule performance index (SPI) = BCWP/BCWS
(Value below 1 indicates that the project is behind schedule.)
* Cost performance index (CPI) = BCWP/ACWP
(CPI<1 then the Project over budgeted)

ety Requirement

any safety standards use the concept of a safety requirement to
Sure that the system carries out the functions needed to make
ceptably safe. For the safety requirements to achieve this (in terms
ne risk reduction is both sufficient and necessary), an adequate risk
sment must have been carried out. Safety requirements may
ale to the frequency of various failure modes of components of a
‘m, any of the other possible layers of protection intended to
Unt a failure from turning into an accident, or processes involved
me development of a system. A safety requirement has two
Penents: a safety functions requirement (which details how the
a Should avoid the occurrence of a hazard), and a safety integrity
“Tement (which details how often the function can fail and allow
A “zard to occur). Between the two components, the safety
-nents for a system state are used to derive how often all the
eo. the system can occur, and from this if the systent
*Plably safe. Some other safety standards are less restrictive
; at 4 safety requirement is, making general statements about
to “quirements being those requirements needed to reduce a
acceptable level. Without adequate iden a ee ae
on of Safety requirements, the system may not be preve

rge number of similar exposure units: Since insurance
“erates through pooling r ssources, the majority of insurance
Pies are provided for individual members of large classes
rowing insurers to benefit from the law of large numbers a
which predicted losses are similar to the actual losses. Exceptions
include Lloyd's of London, which is famous for insuring the life
or health of actors, sports figures, and other famous individuals,
However, all exposures will have particular differences, which
may lead to different premium rates.

A la

Definite loss: The loss takes place at a known time, in a known
place, and from a known cause. The classic example is the death
of an insured person on a life insurance policy. Fire, automobile
accidents, and worker injuries may all easily meet this criterion.
Other types of losses may only be definite in theory. Occupational
disease, for instance, may involve prolonged exposure to injurious
fonditions where no specific time, place, or cause is identifiable.
Ideally, the time, place, and cause of a loss should be clear enough
that a reasonable person, with sufficient information, could
Objectively verify all three elements.

iuntal loss: The event that constitutes the trigger of a claim
benef a : fortuitous, or at least outside the control of the
, a of the insurance. The loss should be pure, in the sense
Or Sie from an event for which there is only the Mia
Otdinary Events that contain speculative elements, sie Ph
Sneral] isiness risks or even purchasing a lottery ticket,
Y not considered insurable.

aggregate shall conform to the requirements of IS 383-1970; 9 :

c) Measurement and Proportioning of C oncrete Materials ms
The aggregate shall be measured by weight or by volume if approved
by the Engineer in a gauge box of correct and approved size based ee
the weight of the material or by other approved accurate means, The
gauge box or another container shall be filled with the aggregate
without compacting to a predetermined uniform depth, accurate
allowance being made for bulking due to a moisture content of the
fine aggregate.

The cement shall be measured by weight, one or more complete bags
containing 50 Kgs being used for a single batch of concrete and as the
size of the mixer shall permit this to be done.

The normal proportions of cement and aggregate shall comply with
the quantities specified below of the concrete described for each part
of the work. The specified quantities shall be altered if instructed after
examination of the aggregate materials in samples or in bulk in order
to obtain the densest concrete with approved materials. Any such
alterations within the range of | part of fine aggregate to 1- 1/2 parts
of coarse aggregate and | part of fine aggregate to 2 -1/2 parts of
coarse aggregate shall be made without any alteration in the rate of
Bill of Quantities.

If the strength of the respective grade concrete does not meet the
compressive strength, the ratio of the cement shall be in

accordingly by trail mix design to meet the minimum compressiv¢
strength of the concrete.

Taxes: Taxes are fixed on the basis of annual rental value
and include municipal tax, property tax, wealth tax which is to
be paid by the owner after deduction of annual repairs.
Repairs: annual repairing cost of the property. Usually 10-15
of gross income or gross rent. For annual repairs generally,
I% to 1.5% of total construction cost is considered.
Management and Collection Charges: 5 to 10 % of gross
ent. This includes the expenses on rent collectors sweeper
i, other overhead expenses.
